ArcSight Console freezes - INC-12872-08102024
Include these emails on allreplies:steven.long@whitlockis.com; support@whitlockis.comContact Phone Number:  888.223.9349 x206 (Email is the bestway to contact me)
Please include INC-12872-08102024 in the subject line of theemail.
We are in the SVI Program and this case should be flagged assuch.  Please make sure this case is flagged as SVI andassigned to 2nd Level Support.
Service: Arcsight ESMVersion: 7.6.4.2772.0
Operating System: Linux (RedHat)OS Version: 7.x
NOTE NOTE NOTE NOTE-------------------
**** THIS IS A U.S. GOVERNMENT/DOD CUSTOMER ****Due to the sensitive nature of the information on thesesystems, please do not request screen sharing, logs,screenshots or access to systems unless the customerexplicitly offers access.
**** Named Support Engineer Contacts ****NSE for ArcSight, David Bush - dbush@opentext.com
-------------------NOTE NOTE NOTE NOTE
Symptoms---------------The ArcSight Console and web ESM are freezing. It fails toload the active channels at times. When it does load, it willeventually freeze and will need the service stopped via theTask Manager. After logging back in, the console (web ESM)works as designed for a few minutes to about an hour at times,then freezes again, preventing one from logging out or clickingon the X to exit the program. This is a major performance issueand prevents the continuous monitoring of the SIEM solutiondue to constant restarts.
Troubleshooting---------------
Client confirms that there were no recent configurationchanges, installations or upgradesClient confirms that event traffic has recently increasedsignificantly
Suggested client delete Cache files and let them beregenerated, no improvementSuggested increasing JVM heap size: Size is set to 1M, noimprovement
Freezes with the following message:Manager Unresponsive:The manager is slow to respond and may be experiencingheavy usage.
Client confirms that additional error messages are show up,stating that it is "unable to find the specified service."
Thanks,Steven Longsteven.long@whitlockis.com

[CAUTION: This email originated from outside of the organization. Do not click links or open attachments unless you recognize the sender and know the content is safe]
Hi Steven,
That's a super common ArcSight pain point. The little 'X' is useless because it only closes the view, it doesn't actually delete the record from ESM.
1. Your counterpart must first ensure that the actual SmartConnector service is stopped (or uninstalled) on the host server. If the connector is running while the resource is deletimmediately attempt to re-register and cause the issue to recur.
2. Log in to the ArcSight ESM Console
3. In the Navigator panel, locate the connector under Resources > Connectors or the specific device group where it resides.
4. Right-click on the disabled SmartConnector resource.
5. Select the option Unregister or Delete.
6. Confirm the deletion when prompted by the system dialog.
Here is a great link to refer to:https://portal.microfocus.com/s/article/KM000010556
Jason[https://urldefense.com/v3/__https://microfocus.my.salesforce.com/servlet/servlet.ImageServer?oid=00D1t000000vhDP&esid=018Q400000K9ITd&from=ext__;!!Obbck6kTJAKYvJieMVSniYsflc8x-8GZy0OXuNtpOq7EAnoP3skco5_5t2R8oeEG6bm28kB0o_liZWn$ ]

Hi Steven,
That's a super common ArcSight pain point. The little 'X' is useless because it only closes the view, it doesn't actually delete the record from ESM.
1. Your counterpart must first ensure that the actual SmartConnector service is stopped (or uninstalled) on the host server. If the connector is running while the resource isdeleted from ESM, it may immediately attempt to re-register and cause the issue to recur.2. Log in to the ArcSight ESM Console3. In the Navigator panel, locate the connector under Resources > Connectors or the specific device group where it resides.4. Right-click on the disabled SmartConnector resource.5. Select the option Unregister or Delete.6. Confirm the deletion when prompted by the system dialog.
Here is a great link to refer to:https://portal.microfocus.com/s/article/KM000010556
Jason[https://urldefense.com/v3/__https://microfocus.my.salesforce.com/servlet/servlet.ImageServer?oid=00D1t000000vhDP&esid=018Q400000K9ITd&from=ext__;!!Obbck6kTJA!diz7Rs9j7OSo8OcXADsIm8YcqptrBJu1cEAs9DChK9cv3i-XaRZ1uq12nN6wrqZ1w3_Y3Ru8zG11kQCSRglFQSdqlh1z4Dw$ ]

Hey Steven,
Thanks for the update and for sending over the version details. That’s helpful.Just to clarify, I only cover ArcSight ESM, so I’ll keep my comments focused there.
ESM Upgrade (7.6.4 → 7.7.0):The jump to 7.7.0 includes some backend performance improvements that could help with the console freezing you’ve been seeing, especially around memory handling,garbage collection, and overall stability. If the issues were tied to ESM response time or backend load, this upgrade may help.
Some Notes
* Memory settings: If you had any custom JVM memory configs set before the upgrade (like in server.wrapper.conf), double-check those post-upgrade. Sometimes upgradesreset them.* Console/ACC responsiveness: Once you're back up and running, let me know how ACC and the thick client behave. If things are still lagging, we may need to do sometuning on the ESM side.* Certs or SSL configs: If anything custom was set up around certs, make sure those come over cleanly during the upgrade.
Once testing is done on your side, let us know how things are performing.

Hey Steven,
Thanks for the update and for sending over the version details. That’s helpful.Just to clarify, I only cover ArcSight ESM, so I’ll keep my comments focused there.
ESM Upgrade (7.6.4 → 7.7.0):The jump to 7.7.0 includes some backend performance improvements that could help with the console freezing you’ve been seeing, especially around memory handling,garbage collection, and overall stability. If the issues were tied to ESM response time or backend load, this upgrade may help.
Some Notes
Memory settings: If you had any custom JVM memory configs set before the upgrade (like in server.wrapper.conf), double-check those post-upgrade. Sometimes upgradesreset them.Console/ACC responsiveness: Once you're back up and running, let me know how ACC and the thick client behave. If things are still lagging, we may need to do some tuningon the ESM side.Certs or SSL configs: If anything custom was set up around certs, make sure those come over cleanly during the upgrade.
Once testing is done on your side, let us know how things are performing.

Hi Steven,
Thanks for the clarification and feedback.
Regarding the question about installing another copy of the Console.The suggestion was to install a second, separate instance of the Console in a different directory on the same VM - not to run two at the same time, but simply to help isolate whethe existing installation path or environment.
As you've noted, much of what's been recommended has already been attempted. However, due to the lack of logs and limited visibility, our ability to pinpoint the root cause is rconsistent freezing behavior across VMs and the absence of similar issues on physical installs, the pattern still strongly suggests something environmental, likely specific to theit's interacting with the Console or Manager.Given the persistent symptoms, the next best step would be to closely review ESM server performance. Indicators such as GC allocation failures and console responsiveness istuning needs, even if services appear up. If Web ESM is also sluggish, that further reinforces the need to assess the backend environment.

Hi Steven,
Thanks for the clarification and feedback.
Regarding the question about installing another copy of the Console.The suggestion was to install a second, separate instance of the Console in a different directory on the same VM — not to run two at the same time, but simply to help isolatewhether the issue might be tied to the existing installation path or environment.
As you’ve noted, much of what’s been recommended has already been attempted. However, due to the lack of logs and limited visibility, our ability to pinpoint the root causeis restricted. Based on the consistent freezing behavior across VMs and the absence of similar issues on physical installs, the pattern still strongly suggests somethingenvironmental, likely specific to the virtual environment or how it’s interacting with the Console or Manager.Given the persistent symptoms, the next best step would be to closely review ESM server performance. Indicators such as GC allocation failures and console responsivenessissues may point to server-side tuning needs, even if services appear up. If Web ESM is also sluggish, that further reinforces the need to assess the backend environment.

Text Body
Hi Steven,
Thanks for the clarification and feedback.
Regarding the question about installing another copy of the Console.The suggestion was to install a second, separate instance of the Console in a different directory on the same VM — not to run two at the same time, but simply to help isolatewhether the issue might be tied to the existing installation path or environment.
As you’ve noted, much of what’s been recommended has already been attempted. However, due to the lack of logs and limited visibility, our ability to pinpoint the root causeis restricted. Based on the consistent freezing behavior across VMs and the absence of similar issues on physical installs, the pattern still strongly suggests somethingenvironmental, likely specific to the virtual environment or how it’s interacting with the Console or Manager.Given the persistent symptoms, the next best step would be to closely review ESM server performance. Indicators such as GC allocation failures and console responsivenessissues may point to server-side tuning needs, even if services appear up. If Web ESM is also sluggish, that further reinforces the need to assess the backend environment.
Jasonref:!00D1t0vhDP.!500Q40DCbFj:ref

Hi Steven,Thanks for the update. After discussing this further with my team, here are the next recommended steps based on their analysis:· Increase the JVM heap size on the VM-based Console installs to 20 GB, as a test to determine if higher allocation reduces the freezing behavior.· Confirm there is no other software running on the same VM that could be competing for resources or interfering with Java processes (e.g., antivirus, endpoint protection,etc.).· Since there’s still no console.log, try installing another copy of the ArcSight Console on the same VM. This will help determine if something in the current installation isbroken or misconfigured.· Review the VM-level resource allocation and template configuration to ensure the VMs are provisioned correctly and consistently.· Finally, if Web ESM/ACC is also performing slowly, that could point to underlying performance issues on the ESM server itself. In that case, additional tuning on the ESMserver may be required.
Jason

Hi Steven,Thanks for the update. After discussing this further with my team, here are the next recommended steps based on their analysis:
Increase the JVM heap size on the VM-based Console installs to 20 GB, as a test to determine if higher allocation reduces the freezing behavior.Confirm there is no other software running on the same VM that could be competing for resources or interfering with Java processes (e.g., antivirus, endpoint protection,etc.).Since there’s still no console.log, try installing another copy of the ArcSight Console on the same VM. This will help determine if something in the current installation isbroken or misconfigured.Review the VM-level resource allocation and template configuration to ensure the VMs are provisioned correctly and consistently.Finally, if Web ESM/ACC is also performing slowly, that could point to underlying performance issues on the ESM server itself. In that case, additional tuning on the ESMserver may be required.

Text Body
Hi Steven,
Thank you again for taking the time to meet with us. Based on our remote session and the limited visibility due to lack of logs or screen sharing, here’s a summary of thefindings.
Summary of Observations:
The slowness issue is isolated to ArcSight Consoles installed on Windows 10 VMs. Physical machine installs do not exhibit this behavior.The affected VMs were previously functional and have been upgraded from 16 GB to 32 GB RAM with 2 CPUs.Occasionally, login to ACC results in the error: "The manager is slow in response. It may be experiencing heavy usage."From the ESM side, the server.std.log shows frequent GC allocation failures and bad timestamp entries from at least one connector (the specific path was identified in logs).Full GC is occurring hourly, which appears normal. However, Java heap size is currently set to 20 GB in server.wrapper.conf, which may be excessive given the working setappears closer to 1 GB.No console.log file was found on either the VM or physical installs.The console's JVM options were initially -Xmx384m. We increased it to -Xmx1024m (no improvement), then to -Xmx4096m, which showed noticeable performanceimprovements.
Next Steps:
Please have additional users update their console memory settings to -Xms512m -Xmx4096m and monitor performance.If performance still lags, consider gradually increasing the max heap size beyond 4 GB and observing impact.Let us know how the updated configuration performs across users and whether any lingering issues persist.
Jasonref:!00D1t0vhDP.!500Q40DCbFj:ref

This wadjusted to accommodate the new JVM settings.      In <INSTALL_DIR>\current\bin\scripts\console.bat adjust this line:      set ARCSIGHT_JVM_OPTIONS=-Xms64m -Xmx512m -XX:-UseThreadPriorities -XX:+HeapDumpOnOutOfMemoryError -Dsun.java2d.noddraw=true -Dcom.sun.xml.bind.v2.bDsun.locale.formatasdefault=true -javaagent:%ARCSIGHT_HOME%\lib\agenthelper-1.1.jar

Hi Steven,Thanks for the update. The fact that the same issue is occurring across all VMs, both new and existing. Strongly suggests this isn’t an isolated installation issue, butsomething broader in the virtual environment.
If multiple, fresh ArcSight Console installs are failing in the same way, that typically points to an environmental issue common to all affected systems.
Local Test (Non-VM Install)If possible, have your counterpart install the ArcSight Console on a non-VM machine, such as:·
* A physical Windows 10 workstation* A system with a different OS image or baselineThis will help us confirm whether the problem is isolated to the VM template/environment. If the console runs properly outside of the VM, we’ll know the virtualizedenvironment is contributing to the failure.
1. Permissions, Antivirus, and Group PoliciesPlease verify the following on one of the VMs:
* The user running the Console has write permissions to the install and log directories* There are no endpoint protection tools, antivirus software, or group policies interfering with Java processes or file I/O* Java is not being sandboxed or restricted by AppLocker or similar controlsWe’ve seen cases where group policies or security tools prevent log files from being created or silently block parts of the application.Jason

Hi Steven,Thanks for the update. The fact that the same issue is occurring across all VMs, both new and existing. Strongly suggests this isn’t an isolated installation issue, butsomething broader in the virtual environment.
If multiple, fresh ArcSight Console installs are failing in the same way, that typically points to an environmental issue common to all affected systems.
Local Test (Non-VM Install)If possible, have your counterpart install the ArcSight Console on a non-VM machine, such as:
A physical Windows 10 workstationA system with a different OS image or baseline
This will help us confirm whether the problem is isolated to the VM template/environment. If the console runs properly outside of the VM, we’ll know the virtualizedenvironment is contributing to the failure.
Permissions, Antivirus, and Group PoliciesPlease verify the following on one of the VMs:
The user running the Console has write permissions to the install and log directoriesThere are no endpoint protection tools, antivirus software, or group policies interfering with Java processes or file I/OJava is not being sandboxed or restricted by AppLocker or similar controls
We’ve seen cases where group policies or security tools prevent log files from being created or silently block parts of the application.Jasonref:!00D1t0vhDP.!500Q40DCbFj:ref

Hi Steven,
Thanks for the update, and I appreciate you checking in with them.
If a fresh install isn't immediately possible, Lets try this.
Ask your counterpart to try launching the console using the command below. This will manually redirect the console's output into a log file.
1. Open Command Prompt as Administrator2. Navigate to the console's scripts folder (adjust the path if needed):cd C:\ArcSight\Console\current\bin\scripts3. Run this command:console.bat > console_output.txt 2>&1
This will create a file named "console_output.txt" in that folder, capturing all startup and runtime messages - including any errors like "Manager Unresponsive."
They can then scroll through that file or provide a few lines around any issues they encounter during or after startup.
If it works, it should give us a clear window into what's happening without needing to wait on a full reinstall.

Hi Steven,
Thanks for your follow-up.
Since the console.log file is still not being created after launching properly with Administrator permissions, the most likely reason is that the ArcSight Console installation onthe VM is either incomplete, corrupted, or missing some expected components.
At this point, to avoid further confusion and to move forward cleanly, the best recommendation is to completely uninstall the ArcSight Console from the VM and reinstall itfresh using a clean installation package.
The reason for this approach is:
* A proper ArcSight Console install automatically creates the logs folder and the console.log file as soon as the console is launched.* If that's not happening, it strongly suggests that part of the installation or environment setup is broken, and continuing to troubleshoot piece-by-piece would likely wastemore time without fully fixing the root cause.
Once the fresh install is completed and the console is launched normally, the console.log file should appear automatically - and from there, we can proceed if any issues stillshow up.
Thank youJason[https://urldefense.com/v3/__https://microfocus.my.salesforce.com/servlet/servlet.ImageServer?oid=00D1t000000vhDP&esid=018Q400000F6R4x&from=ext__;!!Obbck6kTJA!e4cYDqVbrI0rOyUErz5o7adQt0nr7rYEV-VBu_zx-FrMiTutRjxtpP5Lhlm3YQ-NKe8itTIQEmhu7mYQUZsDtqs2HrF7sX8$ ]

Text Body
Hi Steven,
Thanks for your follow-up.
Since the console.log file is still not being created after launching properly with Administrator permissions, the most likely reason is that the ArcSight Console installation onthe VM is either incomplete, corrupted, or missing some expected components.
At this point, to avoid further confusion and to move forward cleanly, the best recommendation is to completely uninstall the ArcSight Console from the VM and reinstall itfresh using a clean installation package.
The reason for this approach is:
A proper ArcSight Console install automatically creates the logs folder and the console.log file as soon as the console is launched.
If that’s not happening, it strongly suggests that part of the installation or environment setup is broken, and continuing to troubleshoot piece-by-piece would likely wastemore time without fully fixing the root cause.
Once the fresh install is completed and the console is launched normally, the console.log file should appear automatically — and from there, we can proceed if any issuesstill show up.
Thank youJasonref:!00D1t0vhDP.!500Q40DCbFj:ref

Hi Steven,
My team suspects the freezing issue is network-related, specifically affecting service calls between the VM-installed ArcSight Console and ESM. To confirm this, pleaseperform the following:
1 - Run the following network tests from the Windows 10 VM:
ping <ESM_IP> -n 50 → Check for packet loss or high latency.tracert <ESM_IP> → Identify how many hops there are to ESM.
2 - Check the ArcSight Console logs for errors:
Navigate to: <console_install_dir>\current\logs\console.logLook for "Manager Unresponsive", "Unable to find the specified service", or any other timeouts/disconnection errors.
3 - Verify network stability:
If the VM is using Wi-Fi, check if it disconnects frequently.If possible, switch to a wired connection and test stability.
Jason

Hi Steven,
Since we haven’t received any further updates from you, we’re proceeding to close this case.
In response to your questions:
1. VM Memory, Disk Space, and CPU Recommendations:For a stable ArcSight Console deployment, it’s important that your VM has sufficient resources. We typically recommend reviewing your current allocation and, if possible,ensuring that the VM is configured with ample memory (often 8 GB or more), adequate CPU cores (at least 4 vCPUs), and enough disk space to handle your workload. Theserecommendations can vary based on your specific environment and usage patterns.2. JVM Heap Size and Configuration File:We suggest increasing the JVM heap size to better support the application’s demands—commonly a minimum of 2 GB, with adjustments up to 4 GB or more as needed. Thesettings for the JVM heap size are defined in the configuration file, which is typically located in your installation’s configuration directory (for example, in[install_directory]/conf/console.conf or a similarly named file). Look for parameters such as -Xms and -Xmx in that file, and adjust them according to your performancerequirements and available VM resources.
It appears that the issues we observed stem from resource constraints on your VM. Please consider making the recommended adjustments to optimize performance.
Jason

02981447-ArcSight Console freezes - INC-12872-08102024 [ ref:!00D1t0vhDP.!500Q40DCbFj:ref ]
Message Date11/8/2024 11:09 AMHas Attachment
Email Addressapagba@opentext.comStatusRepliedSubject02981447-ArcSight Console freezes - INC-12872-08102024 [ ref:!00D1t0vhDP.!500Q40DCbFj:ref ]
Text Body
Hi Steven,
Following Dale’s recommendations, I wanted to pass along the tuning suggestions provided while I was out of the office. These updates should complement the guidancepreviously sent by Bryan. Please review and apply these adjustments to optimize performance across your environment:
Console
Console Memory Allocation:Go to <INSTALL_DIR>\current\bin\scripts and open console.bat. Locate the line:
set ARCSIGHT_JVM_OPTIONS=-Xms64m -Xmx512m -XX:-UseThreadPriorities -XX:+HeapDumpOnOutOfMemoryError -Dsun.java2d.noddraw=true -Dcom.sun.xml.bind.v2.bytecode.ClassTailor.noOptimize=true -Dsun.locale.formatasdefault=true -javaagent:%ARCSIGHT_HOME%\lib\agenthelper-1.1.jar
Update the -Xmx value in line with the available RAM on the console machine. This change will take effect after a console restart.
ESM
Java Heap for Manager Services:In /opt/arcsight/manager/config/server.wrapper.conf, locate:
wrapper.java.maxmemory=16384
Adjust the maxmemory value according to the total RAM, accounting for OS usage. Ensure that initmemory is set lower than maxmemory for optimized memory scaling andminimize garbage collection interruptions.
Logger Heap Usage:In /opt/arcsight/logger/current/arcsight/logger/bin/scripts, edit servers.sh. Locate:
ARCSIGHT_JVM_OPTIONS="-verbose:gc -Xms256m -Xmx4096m -XX:MaxDirectMemorySize=2500M -XX:+HeapDumpOnOutOfMemoryError -Djava.awt.headless=true$ARCSIGHT_PREFERIP"
Set -Xmx based on RAM availability on the server, ensuring adequate memory for OS and ESM needs.
Database Buffer Adjustment:In /opt/arcsight/logger/data/mysql, edit my.cnf and find:
innodb_buffer_pool_size = 512M
Increase this value to between 5-10G, or an amount suitable for the ESM's resources.
Important Note: Remember to back up all files before making changes and restart the ESM services to apply these configurations.
Again, these recommendations are meant to compliment the guidance provided by Bryan.
Please let me know if there are any questions or if further assistance is needed with implementing these adjustments.
Thank you,
Jasonref:!00D1t0vhDP.!500Q40DCbFj:ref

Hi Steven,
Thanks for the update. The information about the physical machine working with a lower Java Heap size (512MB) compared to the VMs (where 3GB seems to be the limit)reinforces the idea that the issue is likely environment-related.
Here's how we can proceed:
1. Investigate Virtualization Resource Allocation:
* Resource Limits: Check the resource allocation settings for the ArcSight VMs within your virtualization platform. Ensure the VMs have sufficient CPU, memory, and disk I/Oallocated to handle the console workload. Compare these settings to the physical machine for reference.
2. Analyze Virtualization Platform Logs:
* Resource Contention: Review logs specific to your virtualization platform (e.g., VMware vSphere logs, Hyper-V logs) for any signs of resource contention. Look for entriesindicating CPU or memory bottlenecks that might be impacting the VMs.
3. Isolate Third-Party Application Interference :
* Temporary Disablement: If possible, temporarily disable any non-essential third-party applications running on the VMs and observe the console behavior. This can helpidentify if a specific application is causing conflicts.
12/11/25, 10:54 AM Case: 02981447 ~ Salesforce - Unlimited Edition
https://microfocus.my.salesforce.com/500Q400000DCbFjIAL/p 66/106
4. Collect ArcSight VM Performance Metrics:
* CPU, Memory, Disk I/O: Monitor CPU usage, memory consumption, and disk I/O activity on the ArcSight VMs while the console freezes or performs poorly. This can helppinpoint potential resource constraints.
Jason

[CAUTION: This email originated from outside of the organization. Do not click links or open attachments unless you recognize the sender and know the content is safe]
1. Locating the ArcSight Server Logs Directory:
* Typically located: The ArcSight server logs are usually found in the /opt/OpenText/ArcSight/ESM/server/logs directory. However, this location might vary depending on yourinstallation.* Check Configuration: If unsure, review the ArcSight Manager configuration files (e.g., arcsight.properties) for any log directory settings.* Use find Command: If you're still unable to locate it, use the find command to search for files with the .log extension.
2. Identifying Relevant Log Files:
* Core Log Files: Focus on files like esm.log, console.log, and manager.log. These contain general information about the ArcSight components.* Channel-Specific Logs: For channel-related issues, check logs with names like channel_name.log. You can find the channel names in the ArcSight Manager.
3. Analyzing Log Files:
* Search for Errors: Look for lines containing the words "ERROR", "WARNING", or "EXCEPTION". 1. Locating the ArcSight Server Logs Directory:
* Typically located: The ArcSight server logs are usually found in the /opt/OpenText/ArcSight/ESM/server/logs directory. However, this location might vary depending on your ins* Check Configuration: If unsure, review the ArcSight Manager configuration files (e.g., arcsight.properties) for any log directory settings.* Use find Command: If you're still unable to locate it, use the find command to search for files with the .log extension.

Hi Steven,
Based on your latest response and our analysis, we've identified a few key areas for potential optimization:
1. Optimize Active Channels:
Review All Active Channels: Please review the list of active channels in the ArcSight Manager. Identify any channels that are no longer necessary or those that might beconsuming excessive resources.Identify Recently Added or Heavily Used Channels: Focus on channels that have been recently added or are being heavily used. These are more likely to be contributing tothe performance issue.Temporarily Disable Channels: If you identify any non-critical channels, consider temporarily disabling them to see if it improves performance. You can re-enable them later ifneeded.Channel Optimization: For channels that remain active, review their configuration. Look for opportunities to optimize queries, reduce data retention periods, or adjustfrequency settings.
2. Memory Optimization:

Subject: 02981447-ArcSight Console freezes - INC-12872-08102024 [ ref:!00D1t0vhDP.!500Q40DCbFj:ref ]Body:Hi Steven,
That's a super common ArcSight pain point. The little 'X' is useless because it only closes the view, it doesn't actually delete the record from ESM. 
Your counterpart must first ensure that the actual SmartConnector service is stopped (or uninstalled) on the host server. If the connector is running while theresource is deleted from ESM, it may immediately attempt to re-register and cause the issue to recur.Log in to the ArcSight ESM ConsoleIn the Navigator panel, locate the connector under Resources > Connectors or the specific device group where it resides.Right-click on the disabled SmartConnector resource.Select the option Unregister or Delete.Confirm the deletion when prompted by the system dialog.
 Here is a great link to refer to:https://portal.microfocus.com/s/article/KM000010556
Jason

Just following up as I haven’t heard back yet regarding the recent memory configuration changes. I wanted to make sure you had the latest feedback in case it didn’tcome through previously.
Based on our review of the behavior and system logs:
The GC allocation failures noted in the server.std.log indicate memory pressure, even with a large heap size.
In some cases, a heap size that’s too large (e.g., 20 GB) can lead to heavier garbage collection overhead, which may impact performance. The actual memory usageappears to be in the 1–2 GB range.
Please continue monitoring how the system performs with the updated console settings (-Xms512m -Xmx4096m) across other users.
If the issue persists, we recommend reviewing the heap size on the manager side as well — reducing it from 20 GB to something in the range of 8–12 GB could helpimprove GC behavior and responsiveness.
Let me know if you’ve seen any changes in performance..

In response to your questions:
VM Memory, Disk Space, and CPU Recommendations:For a stable ArcSight Console deployment, it’s important that your VM has sufficient resources. We typically recommend reviewing your current allocation and, ifpossible, ensuring that the VM is configured with ample memory (often 8 GB or more), adequate CPU cores (at least 4 vCPUs), and enough disk space to handle yourworkload. These recommendations can vary based on your specific environment and usage patterns.
JVM Heap Size and Configuration File:We suggest increasing the JVM heap size to better support the application’s demands—commonly a minimum of 2 GB, with adjustments up to 4 GB or more asneeded. The settings for the JVM heap size are defined in the configuration file, which is typically located in your installation’s configuration directory (for example, in[install_directory]/conf/console.conf or a similarly named file). Look for parameters such as -Xms and -Xmx in that file, and adjust them according to yourperformance requirements and available VM resources.
It appears that the issues we observed stem from resource constraints on your VM. Please consider making the recommended adjustments to optimize performance.

Additional To: apagba@opentext.comCC: steven.long@whitlockis.com; pablo.hernandez@microfocus.com; dbush@opentext.com; support@whitlockis.com; apagba@opentext.com;ddowden@opentext.com; hshi3@opentext.com; jviloria2@opentext.comBCC: jason.viloria@microfocus.comAttachment:
Subject: 02981447-ArcSight Console freezes - INC-12872-08102024 [ ref:!00D1t0vhDP.!500Q40DCbFj:ref ]Body:Hi Steven,
Following Dale’s recommendations, I wanted to pass along the tuning suggestions provided while I was out of the office. These updates should complement theguidance previously sent by Bryan. Please review and apply these adjustments to optimize performance across your environment:
Console
Console Memory Allocation:Go to <INSTALL_DIR>\current\bin\scripts and open console.bat. Locate the line:
set ARCSIGHT_JVM_OPTIONS=-Xms64m -Xmx512m -XX:-UseThreadPriorities -XX:+HeapDumpOnOutOfMemoryError -Dsun.java2d.noddraw=true -Dcom.sun.xml.bind.v2.bytecode.ClassTailor.noOptimize=true -Dsun.locale.formatasdefault=true -javaagent:%ARCSIGHT_HOME%\lib\agenthelper-1.1.jar
Update the -Xmx value in line with the available RAM on the console machine. This change will take effect after a console restart.
ESM 
Java Heap for Manager Services:In /opt/arcsight/manager/config/server.wrapper.conf, locate:
wrapper.java.maxmemory=16384
Adjust the maxmemory value according to the total RAM, accounting for OS usage. Ensure that initmemory is set lower than maxmemory for optimized memoryscaling and minimize garbage collection interruptions.
Logger Heap Usage:In /opt/arcsight/logger/current/arcsight/logger/bin/scripts, edit servers.sh. Locate:
ARCSIGHT_JVM_OPTIONS="-verbose:gc -Xms256m -Xmx4096m -XX:MaxDirectMemorySize=2500M -XX:+HeapDumpOnOutOfMemoryError -Djava.awt.headless=true$ARCSIGHT_PREFERIP"
Set -Xmx based on RAM availability on the server, ensuring adequate memory for OS and ESM needs.
Database Buffer Adjustment:In /opt/arcsight/logger/data/mysql, edit my.cnf and find:
innodb_buffer_pool_size = 512M
Increase this value to between 5-10G, or an amount suitable for the ESM's resources.
Important Note: Remember to back up all files before making changes and restart the ESM services to apply these configurations.
Again, these recommendations are meant to compliment the guidance provided by Bryan.
Please let me know if there are any questions or if further assistance is needed with implementing these adjustments.
Thank you,
Jason

Subject: 02981447-ArcSight Console freezes - INC-12872-08102024 [ ref:!00D1t0vhDP.!500Q40DCbFj:ref ]Body:Hi Steven,
Thanks for the update. The information about the physical machine working with a lower Java Heap size (512MB) compared to the VMs (where 3GB seems to be thelimit) reinforces the idea that the issue is likely environment-related.
Here's how we can proceed:
1. Investigate Virtualization Resource Allocation:
Resource Limits: Check the resource allocation settings for the ArcSight VMs within your virtualization platform. Ensure the VMs have sufficient CPU, memory, anddisk I/O allocated to handle the console workload. Compare these settings to the physical machine for reference.
2. Analyze Virtualization Platform Logs:
Resource Contention: Review logs specific to your virtualization platform (e.g., VMware vSphere logs, Hyper-V logs) for any signs of resource contention. Look forentries indicating CPU or memory bottlenecks that might be impacting the VMs.
3. Isolate Third-Party Application Interference :
Temporary Disablement: If possible, temporarily disable any non-essential third-party applications running on the VMs and observe the console behavior. This canhelp identify if a specific application is causing conflicts.
4. Collect ArcSight VM Performance Metrics:
CPU, Memory, Disk I/O: Monitor CPU usage, memory consumption, and disk I/O activity on the ArcSight VMs while the console freezes or performs poorly. This canhelp pinpoint potential resource constraints.

Then these will override whatever is defined in server.default.wrapper.conf (example: wrapper.java.maxmemory=128)

Allan Pagba Hi David,   Changed ownership as instructed by Dexter.   Thanks, AllanOctober 23, 2025 at 7:51 AM
Link Posts
Dale Dowden Gents,   As discussed, please find some tuning recommendations to go along with what Bryan had previously sent. Please keep in mind, that these recommendations are limited in scope dueto not being able to see the logs and the current configuration.   Console   For all the consoles in your environment, go to <INSTALL_DIR>\current\bin\scripts and edit console.bat. Look for:   setARCSIGHT_JVM_OPTIONS=-Xms64m -Xmx512m -XX:-UseThreadPriorities -XX:+HeapDumpOnOutOfMemoryError -Dsun.java2d.noddraw=true -Dcom.sun.xml.bind.v2.bytecode.ClassTailor.noOptimize=true -Dsun.locale.formatasdefault=true -javaagent:%ARCSIGHT_HOME%\lib\agenthelper-1.1.jar goto jvmOptionsOK   Change the -Xmx value tosomething that makes sense compared to the amount of RAM on the Console machine, whether that be a Virtual Desktop or individual laptops. This change will not take affect until the Console is restarted.  ESM   Java Heap for Manager services   Go to /opt/arcsight/manager/config/server.wrapper.conf   Look for:   wrapper.java.maxmemory=16384   Change the maxmemory value to something that makesense in ESM based off total RAM available. Please keep OS memory usage in mind, when making adjustments here. Also, keep in mind that the higher this value, the longer it will take for Java to GarbageCollect. When Garbage Collection is occurring, there are no events persisting to the database. Ensure that initmemory is lower than maxmemory. This allows Java to increase memory usage as needed.  Logger Heap Usage for Logger services   Go to /opt/arcsight/logger/current/arcsight/logger/bin/scripts and edit servers.sh   Look for:   ARCSIGHT_JVM_OPTIONS="-verbose:gc -Xms256m -Xmx4096m -XX:MaxDirectMemorySize=2500M -XX:+HeapDumpOnOutOfMemoryError -Djava.awt.headless=true $ARCSIGHT_PREFERIP"   Set -Xmx value to something that makes sense for this ESM as it relates tototal RAM available on the server, the amount used by the OS and ESM.   Database Buffer   Go to /opt/arcsight/logger/data/mysql and edit my.cnf   Look for:   innodb_buffer_pool_size = 512M  ß This is theDefault value   Set this to something that makes sense in for this ESM, but usually we see this value set to 5 – 10G.   PLEASE NOTE: These changes will not take effect until the ESM services arerestarted. Also, please backup the files before making changes to that you can revert if needed.   Again, these recommendations are meant to compliment the guidance provided by Bryan.   If I think of anyothers, I will forward along to you.   Thank you,   Dale Dowden Micro Focus Arcsight Support | Micro Focus, an OpenText Company Working hours: 9:00am – 5pm GMT+1 Monday to Thursday   For urgentaccess to our support teams please use our Chat Service or Phone as detailed below: Chat: https://portal.microfocus.com Phone: https://support.microfocus.com/contact/swgrp.html   For comments on oursupport service please contact my manager: Vinod Khushaldasani (vinod.khushaldasani@microfocus.com)  Link attached: https://portal.microfocus.comNovember 1, 2024 at 12:28 PM
